Restrictions in some spots urged even if target met

Publication info: The Age ; Melbourne, Vic. [Melbourne, Vic]. 18 Sep 2021: 4.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/restrictions-some-spots-urged-even-if-target-met/docview/2574674587/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=2203580X&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Restrictions+in+some+spots+urged+even+if+target+met&amp;jtitle=The+Age&amp;pubname=The+Age&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Restrictions+in+some+spots+urged+even+if+target+met&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=4&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: State and territory leaders have been told restrictions including stay-at-home orders and a ban on any travel should remain in areas of concern where thousands of cases are reported each day even when 70 per cent of the eligible population is vaccinated.
Concerns were raised in yesterday's national cabinet meeting about whether the health systems in NSW and Victoria could cope with the ongoing outbreaks. The bulk of the country's more than 1800 cases yesterday were in those states, and there have been 12,519 cases reported over the past week.
So far 45.4 per cent of the eligible population aged 16 and over is fully vaccinated and 70.5 per cent of that population has had one dose, passing a "significant and important" national milestone, Health Minister Greg Hunt said.
"My hope is that everybody, everybody who has not yet taken the vaccine will come forward over the coming days and weeks, and there's sufficient vaccine for every Australian before the end of October, if not significantly earlier," he said.
Under the national plan, restrictions can begin to ease once 70 per cent of the eligible is fully vaccinated, and more freedoms will be introduced once 80 per cent have been double-dosed.
But a sensitivity analysis of the modelling that informed the plan, conducted by the Doherty Institute and presented to state and territory leaders yesterday, found that if daily case numbers were in the thousands it would be prudent to keep "medium" public health safety measures in place in locations of concern until that 80 per cent target is reached.
The Doherty Institute defines medium public health measures as those that were in effect in Sydney on July 1 this year, which include no interstate travel, stay at home except for essential purposes, work from home if possible, but some limited seating for hospitality venues.
The analysis also showed, however, that the original plan to begin transitioning at 70 per cent fully vaccinated remained broadly robust even if an outbreak started with thousands of cases.
Given the pace of the vaccination rollout, the federal government estimates it will take two weeks for the double-dosed vaccination rate to go from 70 per cent to 80 per cent.
As most of the country begins to look towards opening up, all state and territory leaders agreed to integrate vaccination certificates with check-in apps so greater freedoms can be considered for the fully vaccinated.
More states have also begun trials of home quarantine as Prime Minister Scott Morrison said the hotel quarantine system had a "use-by date", and national cabinet discussed making vaccinations mandatory for all healthcare workers across the country.
GPs in every state and territory bar NSW, Victoria and the ACT can book over-60s for Pfizer vaccines, and President of the Royal Australian College of General Practitioners Dr Karen Price said the federal government should make that a national guideline.
"That would be really smart," she said, but emphasised it was important that Pfizer bookings for over-60s were not prioritised over other vulnerable groups. "What I hope it means is there's a turning of the tide in terms of supply."
The supply of mRNA vaccines is rapidly increasing. September's doses have been doubled from initial forecasts to roughly 11 million doses of both the Pfizer and Moderna vaccines.
Doctors in Queensland, Western Australia, the Northern Territory, South Australia and Tasmania will soon be able to administer Pfizer to patients aged 60 and over after those states changed their eligibility criteria. Across the country, roughly 470,000 people aged 60 and up are yet to have a first dose.
A spokesman from Operation COVID Shield said the national policy - which states AstraZeneca is the preferred vaccine for people aged 60 and over, and Pfizer should be used in people aged under 60 - hasn't changed, but as long as primary care providers were not turning down priority patients (including 12 to 15-year-olds and pregnant women) they could match state guidelines on vaccinations.
After Queensland announced it would open up Pfizer doses in its state-run hubs for over-60s, the state's Health Minister Yvette D'Ath said the government wanted to make sure people had choices.
"The Morrison government promised people over 60 that later in the year they would be given a choice of vaccines," she told reporters yesterday. With Matt Dennien

Premiers unite on over-60s

Publication info: Herald Sun ; Melbourne, Vic. [Melbourne, Vic]. 18 Sep 2021: 6.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/premiers-unite-on-over-60s/docview/2573616633/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=10383433&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Premiers+unite+on+over-60s&amp;jtitle=Herald+Sun&amp;pubname=Herald+Sun&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Premiers+unite+on+over-60s&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=6&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: PREMIERS Daniel Andrews and Gladys Berejiklian have teamed up in national cabinet to pour cold water on the plan by their Queensland counterpart Annastacia Palaszczuk to give Pfizer vaccines to the over-60s.
Instead the pair argued they would wait at least ­another fortnight while other priority groups were given Pfizer.
The refusal is in contrast to Queensland’s plan to make Pfizer available immediately to people over 60, a move that has been criticised because it may see AstraZeneca vaccines go to waste.
Friday afternoon’s national cabinet meeting ticked off on a national code on boarding school students that will allow them and their parents and carers – as well as boarding school staff – to travel across borders between school and home.
Regional Education Minister Bridget McKenzie called on all jurisdictions to quickly ­implement the plan to help 23,000 students and their families travel during the school holidays.
“While border closures and intrastate travel restrictions have helped contain the spread of Covid-19, it has unintentionally left some boarding students isolated and unable to receive the support and care of family, causing additional stress and anxiety,” she said.
“Today’s decision is a win for commonsense.” National cabinet also received an update from Professor Jodie McVernon, of the Doherty Institute, and top bureaucrat Phil Gaetjens on ­reopening modelling. It confirmed Doherty’s analysis that the Delta variant could be managed when ­between 70 and 80 per cent of the population aged over 16 had been fully vaccinated.

Dan and Gladys unite to reject over-60 Pfizer plan

Publication info: Geelong Advertiser ; Geelong, Vic. [Geelong, Vic]. 18 Sep 2021: 9.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/dan-gladys-unite-reject-over-60-pfizer-plan/docview/2573614186/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=13246216&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Dan+and+Gladys+unite+to+reject+over-60+Pfizer+plan&amp;jtitle=Geelong+Advertiser&amp;pubname=Geelong+Advertiser&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Dan+and+Gladys+unite+to+reject+over-60+Pfizer+plan&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=9&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: PREMIERS Daniel Andrews and Gladys Berejiklian have teamed up in national cabinet to pour cold water on the plan by their Queensland counterpart Annastacia Palaszczuk to give Pfizer vaccines to the over-60s.
Instead, the respective Victorian and NSW leaders agreed to wait at least ­another fortnight while other priority groups were given Pfizer jabs.
The refusal contrasts with Queensland’s plan to make Pfizer available immediately to people over 60, a move criticised because it may result in AstraZeneca vaccines going to waste.
Friday afternoon’s national cabinet meeting ticked off on a national code on boarding school students that will allow them and their parents and carers – as well as staff – to travel across borders between school and home. Federal Regional Education Minister Bridget McKenzie called on all juris­dictions to quickly ­implement the plan to help 23,000 students and their families travel during the school holidays.
“While border closures and intrastate travel restrictions have helped contain the spread of Covid-19, it has unintentionally left some boarding students isolated and unable to receive the support and care of family, causing additional stress and anxiety,” she said.
“(This) decision is a win for common sense.” National cabinet also received an update from Professor Jodie McVernon, of the Doherty Institute, and top bureaucrat Phil Gaetjens on ­reopening modelling.
It confirmed the institute’s analysis that the Delta variant could be managed when ­between 70 and 80 per cent of the population aged over 16 had been fully vaccinated, when combined with testing, tracing, isolation and quarantine regimens. The meeting also agreed all jurisdictions would work to integrate people’s immunisation history into state and territory check-in apps that could be used to comply with public health orders.

Open up at 80pc: Donato

Publication info: Forbes Advocate ; Forbes, N.S.W. [Forbes, N.S.W]. 17 Sep 2021: 5.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/open-up-at-80pc-donato/docview/2573007462/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=13289632&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Open+up+at+80pc%3A+Donato&amp;jtitle=Forbes+Advocate&amp;pubname=Forbes+Advocate&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Open+up+at+80pc%3A+Donato&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=5&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Donato calls for restrictions to go at 80 per cent vaccinations
All COVID restrictions should be lifted when 80 per cent of the local population is double vaccinated.
That's the view of the member for Orange Phil Donato who has called on the state government to provide a more-detailed roadmap for the future once people are vaccinated.
Mr Donato said the restrictions should be lifted across the state once 80 per cent of NSW residents were double-dosed.
But he said if a local government area reached that level before other areas, residents should then be allowed full freedom from restrictions.
And he said the government should not be able to reintroduce health restrictions once the 80 per cent target was reached.
"The government says they 'intend to open up further freedoms' when hit 80 per cent double-dose vaccinations, flagging there will be ongoing health order restrictions beyond that point," he said.
"Freedom doesn't come with terms and conditions or strings attached. We don't want them to keep moving the goalposts."
Mr Donato said the government also needed to clarify what restrictions would be lifted when 70 per cent vaccinations were reached.
"We now know (the premier's) 70 per cent goal is no real freedom at all, with many restrictions remaining," he said.
Mr Donato said community sport would still not be allowed and businesses would face social distancing restrictions limiting how many people they could have at their venues depending on the floor size.
He said an Orange hairdresser had told him they would not re-open with those limits in place.
Mr Donato said he did not support a COVID passport, which keeps restrictions in place for the unjabbed.
He said it was up to people to decide whether to get vaccinated and those that didn't get vaccinated ran the risk of getting sick or dying.
"I'm not a supporter of vaccine passports," he said. "The reality of policing it is going to be very difficult."
Mr Donato said the state government should follow the Doherty Institute's modelling which showed the rate of COVID transmission fell when the 80 per cent target was reached.
"Given this is the accepted measure, 80 per cent vaccination is the official high target and therefore the point at which society should resume normality, free of health order restrictions," he said.
"I'm calling on the Premier to make a commitment to the community of NSW that she lifts all health order restrictions and return our freedoms, unconditionally, upon reaching the goal of 80 per cent double-dose vaccination of the adult population."
He said the uncertainty of the current situation was impacting businesses, costing people their jobs and putting people under stress leading to mental health problems.
Mr Donato also called on the government to re-open state parliament which is currently closed due to the pandemic.
He said parliament provided opportunities for state members to put the government under scrutiny.
CREDIT: David Fitzsimons

Subject: State government; Immunization

____________________________________________________________

Shire Matters with Mark Speakman: Reopening NSW roadmap offers light at the end of the tunnel

Publication info: St. George and Sutherland Shire Leader ; Rockdale, N.S.W. [Rockdale, N.S.W]. 17 Sep 2021: 0.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/shire-matters-with-mark-speakman-reopening-nsw/docview/2573006033/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Shire+Matters+with+Mark+Speakman%3A+Reopening+NSW+roadmap+offers+light+at+the+end+of+the+tunnel&amp;jtitle=St.+George+and+Sutherland+Shire+Leader&amp;pubname=St.+George+and+Sutherland+Shire+Leader&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Shire+Matters+with+Mark+Speakman%3A+Reopening+NSW+roadmap+offers+light+at+the+end+of+the+tunnel&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=0&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Life at 70 per cent and 80 per cent double-dose vaccination will be a lot different than it is now. Every day, we're inching closer to those important targets and to a more normal way of life.
Under the Reopening NSW roadmap announced last week, many restrictions to gathering, movement, retail and hospitality will be eased for fully vaccinated people (as well as those
with medical exemptions) when our state hits 70 per cent adult coverage.
It means we'll be able to gather with our families and friends. We'll be able to dine out or enjoy a beer at the pub. We'll be able to exercise at gyms, get a haircut, attend church services, enjoy a bit of retail therapy, or take a weekend trip away. There's light at the end of the tunnel.
If you haven't received your first vaccine dose, I strongly encourage you to book an appointment as soon as you can. This is largely a pandemic of the unvaccinated.
Vaccination protects you from severe disease, hospitalisation and death; the vast majority of deaths and ICU admissions in the current outbreak have been unvaccinated. Vaccination also protects the people around you by limiting the possibility for onward virus transmission.
For the time being, to open up for unvaccinated people would overwhelm our health system and produce many thousands of deaths. This point is underscored by recent modelling by the Burnet Institute, which shows that the current lockdown measures in New South Wales, combined with targeted vaccination, may have prevented more than 580,000 cases and 5,800 deaths.
The roadmap is subject to further fine-tuning and to health advice if circumstances change drastically or if cases within a designated area remain too high. But clearly, the higher our vaccination rates, the stronger our collective armour as we adjust to living with COVID.
It's no surprise that Sutherland Shire residents have been rolling up their sleeves and doing their share of heavy lifting. Ours is the third most vaccinated statistical area in NSW. Let's keep getting those rates as high as we possibly can, so we can get back to doing all the things we love.
In the meantime, please look out for each other and stay safe.
CREDIT:

____________________________________________________________

Hope on the horizon if we all do our bit

Publication info: Port Stephens Examiner ; Raymond Terrace, N.S.W. [Raymond Terrace, N.S.W]. 16 Sep 2021: 15.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/hope-on-horizon-if-we-all-do-our-bit/docview/2572596840/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Hope+on+the+horizon+if+we+all+do+our+bit&amp;jtitle=Port+Stephens+Examiner&amp;pubname=Port+Stephens+Examiner&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Hope+on+the+horizon+if+we+all+do+our+bit&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=15&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Lockdown has been horrible, but there is hope on the horizon.
The NSW Government has announced that restrictions will ease for vaccinated people once our State reaches the 70 per cent double dose threshold.
When we emerge from lockdown, our collective goal must be to keep our hard-fought freedoms.
So, it is vital that we have all the protections in place before we emerge, to keep our community safe when we do. We must minimise the risk of an uncontrolled COVID-19 outbreak in Port Stephens - which could see the reintroduction of harsh lockdown rules.
And here lies the challenge.
When restrictions ease, Port Stephens will be hit by a tsunami of Sydneysiders and other travellers longing for our beautiful beaches, Summer sun and fresh air.
For local businesses and workers, visitors will be very welcome. But the complexity that lies ahead is mind boggling. Can they serve unvaccinated customers? Can they operate with unvaccinated staff? Are they obliged to enforce vaccination rules, and if so, how? Will they continue receiving financial support if their wages or profits are impacted by the rules?
Our community requires clear answers from the Government to ensure our collective relief after escaping lockdown isn't replaced with anxiety.
I've asked the NSW Government to work with our community to create a strong plan with clear rules to ensure we stay safe and our freedoms remain. Our community deserves to have predictable problems resolved prior to opening up, rather than waiting for a crisis to unfold.
I have sought a proactive expansion of local healthcare services so they don't become overwhelmed if cases climb.
Importantly, the Doherty Modelling Report has shown that further lockdowns can be avoided if our contact tracing system is strong.
Too often in Port Stephens, we have seen significant delays in exposure sites being published by Health authorities, despite their best efforts. These delays will have serious consequences once restrictions have eased, so I have requested the Government strengthen the capacity of our local contact tracing team.
But the first and best line of defence remains vaccination, especially for our tourism and hospitality workers who will become another frontline workforce - face to face with visitors from across the State.
Frustratingly, the Morrison Government's failed vaccine rollout could quickly become a handbrake on our personal freedom, with many locals still unable to access the vaccines they need.
However, I'm hopeful that the much-promised vaccine supply will appear soon and everyone will get their opportunity to protect themselves, their loved ones and our community.
So, in the coming weeks, it's critical that we keep working together as a community to get ourselves safely out of lockdown and, importantly, staying there. Let's hope the government plays its part as well.
Kate Washington MP is the Member for Port Stephens and the Shadow Minister for Family and Community Services.
CREDIT:

Subject: Vaccines; Immunization; Contact tracing

Herald Sun

Publication info: Herald Sun ; Melbourne, Vic. [Melbourne, Vic]. 14 Sep 2021: 20.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/herald-sun/docview/2572060936/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=10383433&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Herald+Sun&amp;jtitle=Herald+Sun&amp;pubname=Herald+Sun&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Herald+Sun&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=20&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Catch NSW on the vaccine gap PREMIER Daniel Andrews needs to adopt the New South Wales reopening model for when a 70 per cent double-dose vaccine target is reached.
While states and territories will hit their national road map trigger points on various dates, Australia needs to have a unified view on what reopening means.
As the most populous states and those carrying the biggest Covid burden, Victoria and NSW need to be on the same page for managing the pandemic and rebooting their respective economies as the nation’s engine rooms.
Keeping on the same page means Victoria must use the next fortnight’s vaccination blitz across Melbourne’s northern and western suburb hot spots to close the gap on Sydney’s lead in vaccination rates.
On the current trajectory, NSW will hit its 70 per cent double-dose vaccination coverage a full two weeks before Victoria.
The major reason for higher rates north of the Murray had been the bolstered Pfizer stocks sent in to combat their rocketing west and southwestern Sydney outbreaks and the push-factor high levels of transmission had on people coming forward for their vaccinations.
This week and next, Victoria will see a major boost in access to the national Pfizer stocks and the later arrival of Moderna will help protect the state’s adolescent population.
While areas of Sydney yesterday relaxed some outdoor, picnic and exercise restrictions for fully vaccinated people (who are required to have proof of vaccination with them), the first significant changes to reopening will occur when 70 per cent are fully vaccinated — a level forecast to be reached in just over a month’s time on October 17.
NSW Premier Gladys Berejiklian has committed to a capped reopening of hospitality, retail, return to work, gyms, outdoor events, social gathering and family reunions and an end to stay-at-home rules from that trigger point for people who have received both doses of the vaccine.
Face-to-face learning in schools in NSW is scheduled to restart on October 25 — while our Premier is yet to clarify what happens in education here.
Premier Berejiklian reiterated yesterday the coming freedoms would be for those fully vaccinated — and those unvaccinated could not expect the same opportunities.
The same messages about freedoms won through vaccinations have been given in this state.
Premier Andrews said Victoria’s road map would be informed by modelling now being finalised by the Burnet Institute and a clear plan will be announced in a week, including full clarity on returning to school.
In coming days, the Premier has also committed to setting out clear rules for vaccinating sectors of the workforce, and requirements for teachers are expected to be included.
But the Premier should also commit to a strategy where, under the soon-to-be-established significant federal expansion of GP and pharmacy vaccination sites, Victoria catches up to NSW on vaccination rates.
If lost ground is not recovered, NSW will also meet its 80 per cent fully vaccinated trigger point under the national cabinet reopening plan on October 31, almost three weeks before Victoria hits the milestone, on or about November 19.
More than 500,000 Victorians were vaccinated last week, meaning we will soon reach the 70 per cent first-dose target, so our travel from home distances will be increased to 10km, we get an extra hour of outdoor exercise and further childminding provisions for essential workers.
But these tweaks are minor at best and Mr Andrews needs to expand relaxation in other areas for those vaccinated now.
Golden Aussie triumph INSPIRATIONAL Melburnian Dylan Alcott has now achieved sporting history with a “Golden Slam” win after being crowned in the US Open.
The only other tennis great to achieve the singles feat — victory at all four Grand Slams plus Olympic gold — was Steffi Graf in 1988.
Novak Djokovic was looking to emulate that record for a calendar year’s competition but lost in his Olympic semi-final bid.
Now it is Alcott who has the rare acclaim after winning the US Open quad singles title to achieve the first men’s Golden Slam in tennis history.
Despite his utter dominance in the sport with 15 grand slams, the emotions and the significance of the moment was clear at Louis Armstrong Stadium in Flushing Meadows.
Cheers were also sent across the Pacific for Samantha Stosur, who with China’s Zhang Shuai, won the US Open women’s doubles title on Sunday and captured her fourth career grand slam doubles title.
Then there was the top podium finish in Monza as Aussie ace Daniel Ricciardo won the Italian Grand Prix with a sensational performance.
It was the eighth victory of Ricciardo’s F1 career but the first since Monaco in 2018 and was McLaren’s first race win since 2012. These Australians have proven once more why we are such a proud and passionate sporting nation.

Donato calls for freedom at 80 per cent

Publication info: Central Western Daily ; Orange, N.S.W. [Orange, N.S.W]. 14 Sep 2021: 6.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/donato-calls-freedom-at-80-per-cent/docview/2571962585/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=13290568&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Donato+calls+for+freedom+at+80+per+cent&amp;jtitle=Central+Western+Daily&amp;pubname=Central+Western+Daily&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Donato+calls+for+freedom+at+80+per+cent&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=6&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: FROM FRONT PAGE Mr Donato said the state government should follow the Doherty Institute's modelling which showed the rate of COVID transmission fell when the 80 per cent target was reached.
"Given this is the accepted measure, 80 per cent vaccination is the official high target and therefore the point at which society should resume normality, free of health order restrictions," he said.
"I'm calling on the Premier to make a commitment to the community of NSW that she lifts all health order restrictions and return our freedoms, unconditionally, upon reaching the goal of 80 per cent double-dose vaccination of the adult population."
He said the uncertainty of the current situation was impacting businesses, costing people their jobs and putting people under stress leading to mental health problems.
Mr Donato also called on the government to re-open state parliament which is currently closed due to the pandemic.
He said parliament provided opportunities for state members to put the government under scrutiny and be held accountable.
And he has questioned why Premier Gladys Berejiklian has called off her daily 11am COVID update press conferences.
CREDIT: David Fitzsimons

LETTERS TO THE EDITOR

Publication info: The Australian ; Canberra, A.C.T. [Canberra, A.C.T]. 09 Sep 2021: 10.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/letters-editor/docview/2570216215/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=unknown&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=10388761&amp;isbn=&amp;title=LETTERS+TO+THE+EDITOR&amp;jtitle=The+Australian&amp;pubname=The+Australian&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=LETTERS+TO+THE+EDITOR&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=10&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: We have become the most divided country in the world The news from the UK (“Britain carefree as Covid rates rise”, 8/9) shows the way for Australia. Despite having an 80 per cent full and 90 per cent part adult vaccination rate, there are still about 40,000 new cases a day. But, and this is the point, the hospital system is not overwhelmed and the average death rate is fewer than 100 per day, almost entirely unvaccinated and far fewer than the usual causes of death.
The effectiveness of the now-cancelled masks and social distancing is called into question, as are the inaccurate modelling predictions of doom. This Delta variant is more infectious but less deadly and we can safely open up as vaccination rates rise.
Dr Graham Pinn, Maroochydore, Qld
The management of the pandemic in Australia can be described only as dysfunctional and chaotic. We have some premiers still clinging to the delusional aspiration of the elimination of the virus. We have others hiding behind “the best medical advice” to justify lockdowns and draconian restrictions on freedom when between the states and territories the “best” advice is inconsistent if not contradictory.
We don’t know if the magical vaccination threshold is 70, 80, 90 or 100 per cent. We don’t know what vaccines are said to be safe at what age. We don’t know how long the vaccines remain effective.
No one dares to question the epidemiological credentials of the so-called experts. In South Australia our expert has a background as a paediatrician. There is simply no consensus as to the way out of the pandemic.
All of this with a national population that is less than that of many cities around the world.
It all goes to show how divided and over-governed we are. Any remaining suggestion that “we are all in this together” is nonsense. We are the laughing stock of the rest of the world.
Geoff Forbes, Kensington Gardens, SA
I am one Aussie with grateful thanks for a PM who works day and night in torrid circumstances. He must endure the petty slings and arrows of those on the left, those who don’t like to be personally inconvenienced and the plain stupid. After all that he does internationally, strategically, locally, under constant fire with the demands of leadership, surely he is entitled to include a visit to his distant children and aged parents with two necessary work appearances in NSW on Father’s Day.
If we keep up this juvenile narcissism towards our leaders, we will never get a normal decent family man to enter politics.
Judy Crooke, Claremont, WA
The recent hysterical outbursts from certain premiers over vaccine allocation must surely rank as one of the uglier and more unedifying examples of populist base politics witnessed in recent times, and that’s saying something. People in western and southwestern Sydney are dying. Outside the southeast corner of NSW, Victoria and the ACT, the country is virtually Covid free and nobody is dying. To vaccinate people in Rockhampton or Albany at the expense of vaccines reaching those in Campsie and Yagoona is nothing short of criminal.
Shayne Thompson, Queens Park, NSW
As Janet Albrechtsen says, serious mental health tragedies are unfolding due to Covid restrictions (“Come to the party, Santa Claus, and reopen the border”, 8/9). Spare a thought for women who have just had their first baby (particularly in Victoria) and are sent home from hospital after only a few hours to a partner with no experience with a newborn, and no relative permitted to cross borders or other visitors allowed. No one to share the joy or to help. Should we be surprised at the increase in postnatal depression that will surely ensue?
Roseanne Schneider, Toowoomba, Qld
Never in living memory have we been such a divided country. The only time we become parochial about our states is when there are football grand finals or State of Origin matches. Any other time when there has been natural disasters such as bushfires, floods or cyclones we rally to support each other and that is the thing I love about Australia.
It is unbelievable that during the worst pandemic the world has experienced in 100 years we are now the most divided country in the world. Glenys Clift, Toowoomba, Qld

Claim 5800 lives saved

Publication info: The Daily Telegraph ; Surry Hills, N.S.W. [Surry Hills, N.S.W]. 08 Sep 2021: 4.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/claim-5800-lives-saved/docview/2569826708/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=18360203&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Claim+5800+lives+saved&amp;jtitle=The+Daily+Telegraph&amp;pubname=The+Daily+Telegraph&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Claim+5800+lives+saved&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=4&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: MORE than 5800 people would have died from Covid-19 by the end of the year if the NSW government did not implement any restrictions or ramp up vaccinations in 12 Sydney hotspots.
New modelling from the Burnet Institute revealed that without any restrictions or the additional Pfizer doses, there would have been almost 590,000 total infections and 5808 deaths. It is projected that the original vaccine rollout and restrictions combined helped save 4830 lives while the addition of 530,000 Pfizer doses saved a further 254 lives.

Claim 5800 lives saved

Publication info: The Daily Telegraph ; Surry Hills, N.S.W. [Surry Hills, N.S.W]. 08 Sep 2021: 4.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/claim-5800-lives-saved/docview/2569825449/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=18360203&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Claim+5800+lives+saved&amp;jtitle=The+Daily+Telegraph&amp;pubname=The+Daily+Telegraph&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Claim+5800+lives+saved&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=4&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: MORE than 5800 people would have died from Covid-19 by the end of the year if the NSW government did not implement any restrictions or ramp up vaccinations in 12 Sydney hotspots.
New modelling from the Burnet Institute revealed that without any restrictions or the additional Pfizer doses, there would have been almost 590,000 total infections and 5808 deaths. It is projected that the original vaccine rollout and restrictions combined helped save 4830 lives while the addition of 530,000 Pfizer doses saved a further 254 lives.

Vaccine supply set for major shot in the arm

Publication info: Newcastle Herald ; Newcastle, N.S.W. [Newcastle, N.S.W]. 08 Sep 2021: 9.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/vaccine-supply-set-major-shot-arm/docview/2569679724/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=22028021&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Vaccine+supply+set+for+major+shot+in+the+arm&amp;jtitle=Newcastle+Herald&amp;pubname=Newcastle+Herald&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Vaccine+supply+set+for+major+shot+in+the+arm&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=9&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Australia's vaccine supply issues are over and the success of the nation's rollout now hinges on public uptake, the man tasked with leading it says.
COVID-19 Taskforce Commander Lieutenant-General John Frewen has also told Australian Community Media the publisher of the Newcastle Herald, that vaccination rates among Indigenous Australians must be accelerated to avoid leaving them exposed once restrictions begin to ease.
The early stages of Australia's rollout were wracked by an undersupply of Pfizer, a problem compounded by the Australian Technical Advisory Group on Immunisation advising against the use of AstraZeneca in people under 60.
But with an imminent influx of mRNA vaccines, General Frewen said Australia was on track to ramp up its rollout in September, a month earlier than initially expected.
"This takes us beyond the phase in the vaccine [rollout] where we were really mRNA supply constrained. The vaccines are coming, the distribution networks are in place and expanding. It all comes down now to public willingness to come forward," he said.
"Sentiment remains strong and high, which is pleasing. But I'm not counting any chickens until we've got everybody through the door. We've still got a ways to go to get us to 70 per cent, and international experience tells us you've got work hard between 70 per cent and 80 per cent."
The federal government last week confirmed it had agreed a vaccine swap with the UK for four million Pfizer doses, the first batch arriving on Sunday. Australia would return the doses by December, General Frewen predicted.
It followed a similar agreement with Singapore for 500,000 doses, and the federal government purchasing an additional one million from Poland. General Frewen said the deals, coupled with the imminent availability of the Moderna jab, would allow the country's remaining GPs to administer mRNA vaccines.
"[That] is going to help us ramp up through September in ways that we didn't think would be possible until October," he said.
"We've got every opportunity, provided people keep stepping forward. So I really encourage everybody who hasn't made a booking to get in and make one now."
The nation's reopening plan, based on modelling by the Doherty Institute, saw Australia begin to reopen once 70 per cent of each state and territory was fully-vaccinated. That did not include 12- to 15-year-olds, who were all eligible to make a booking from Monday.
Nor did it include a minimum threshold for Indigenous and Torres Strait Islander Australians, raising the prospect of Australia opening up while they remained vulnerable.
Just over 40 per cent of Aboriginal and Torres Strait Islander Australians aged 16 and over had received a first dose by Monday, well below the broader population of 63 per cent. Just 23 per cent were fully vaccinated, compared to 38 per cent nationally.
General Frewen conceded vaccination among First Nations peoples had fallen behind early in the rollout and, although it had doubled in the last month, the rate was still only keeping pace with the rest of Australia.
"So we've got to accelerate it to catch it up, because we don't want them to be behind when the rest of the nation gets to 70 and 80 per cent," he said.
"We're going to accelerate where we can over the next month by focusing on some of those communities that are most behind right now."
General Frewen would not predict when the Indigenous population would hit 70 per cent, warning vaccine hesitancy would prove the "ultimate variable".
He warned a relatively COVID-free existence in most remote communities, some of which had vaccination rates under 10 per cent, had caused complacency over the vaccine.
But the virus' spread through regional NSW, including the first deaths among Indigenous Australians, had prompted a shift in the region.
Work was being done with local leaders and trusted community identities to counter disinformation, he said.
"[They are] stressing not only that the vaccines are safe and important, but there is a real urgency to this," he said.
"Western NSW has given us a good reminder that COVID can rip into these communities really quickly, so we're better to get in and get ahead of the curve."
CREDIT: Finn McHugh

It’s a jabs rate race to stall inevitable

Publication info: The Australian ; Canberra, A.C.T. [Canberra, A.C.T]. 06 Sep 2021: 5.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/s-jabs-rate-race-stall-inevitable/docview/2569273410/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=10388761&amp;isbn=&amp;title=It%E2%80%99s+a+jabs+rate+race+to+stall+inevitable&amp;jtitle=The+Australian&amp;pubname=The+Australian&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=It%26rsquo%3Bs+a+jabs+rate+race+to+stall+inevitable&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=5&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Queensland is racing against the clock to boost lagging vaccination rates as it teeters on the edge of another lockdown, with Annastacia Palaszczuk warning that Covid would spread through the state “sometime in the near ­future”.
The Queensland Premier held off on locking down the state at the weekend but remains “concerned” about a group of people exposed to the Delta variant at a nail salon in Logan, south of Brisbane, last week.
Contact tracers are still “struggling” to track down the group who visited the salon at the same time as a Covid-infected truck driver.
“It is imperative you get vaccinated because this virus will pop up in the near future,” Ms Palas­zczuk said.
“I cannot stress to you enough … if you’re sitting at home and you’re thinking, well, I might just wait, don’t wait.
“Every single person that gets vaccinated is protecting us from having a huge outbreak.” As of Saturday, 34 per cent of eligible Queenslanders were double-dosed compared with 45 per cent in Tasmania and the ACT.
In NSW, 40 per cent of the eligible population is fully vaccinated, as the state added another 1485 cases to its Covid tally on Sunday and three deaths.
Seventy per cent of the eligible population has received one dose of the vaccine, which Gladys Bere­jiklian said was “pleasing”.
The NSW Premier blasted other state leaders who had not committed to reopening state borders even when Australia reached its 80 per cent vaccination target.
“Once we hit 80 per cent double dose, all internal borders in Australia should not exist and by that stage NSW would welcome home thousands of Australians every week,” Ms Bere­jiklian said.
“We certainly will not have to have a statewide lockdown ever again when we hit the 80 per cent double-dose vaccination rate, which is what we’re looking forward to.
She warned other state leaders that a major outbreak was imminent, urging them to stick to the national plan.
“NSW has had to confront some issues because a major outbreak happened here first but other states will have to go through this,” she said.
“Victoria is going through it. If you follow the rate of cases at the time we had ours, you will see the pattern.” Ms Palaszczuk said she was “trying so hard” to move the state’s border checkpoint further south to allow families to reunite, and was continuing discussions with her NSW counterpart.
Separated families gathered along the Queensland-NSW ­border on Father’s Day to share hugs and kisses, despite stay-at-home orders for all NSW ­residents.
Crowds of up to 200 gathered along barricades and Acting Chief Superintendent Rhys Wildman said police took a “compassionate” approach by handing out several hundred masks rather than fines.
In Victoria, another 183 infections were reported as Premier Daniel Andrews said it was ­“highly likely” a wide range of public events would be open only to vaccinated people once 80 per cent of Victorians had had two doses.
“We are going to move from a situation where to protect the health system we have everybody locked down … to a situation where to protect the health system we are going to lock out ­people who are not vaccinated and can be,” he said.
“If you’re making the choice not to get vaccinated, then you are making the wrong choice.” Mr Andrews said people concerned about the impact of corona­virus on children once Australia reopened should be aware that those aged under 12 were considered in the Doherty Institute modelling that formed the basis for national cabinet’s recommendation of achieving 70 per cent and 80 per cent vaccination thresholds.
CREDIT: Lydia Lynch; Ellie Dudley

Hunt backs jabs for over-12s despite doubts

Publication info: Sun Herald ; Sydney, N.S.W. [Sydney, N.S.W]. 05 Sep 2021: 8.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/hunt-backs-jabs-over-12s-despite-doubts/docview/2569048441/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=13231987&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Hunt+backs+jabs+for+over-12s+despite+doubts&amp;jtitle=Sun+Herald&amp;pubname=Sun+Herald&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Hunt+backs+jabs+for+over-12s+despite+doubts%3A+exclusive&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=8&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Federal Health Minister Greg Hunt has reassured Australian parents the government's decision to vaccinate 12- to 15-year-olds is based on the best health advice and will get kids back to school sooner, after a British expert group recommended against vaccinating healthy adolescents.
A week after Australia approved vaccination of children as young as 12, the UK's Joint Committee on Vaccination and Immunisation said the benefits of doing so were only "marginally greater than the potential known harms".
"It is not within the JCVI's remit to consider the wider societal impacts of vaccination, including educational benefits," the body noted in a decision that shocked experts and which is at odds with moves by Australia, the US, Canada, Israel and many European countries to vaccinate children aged 12 and over.
UK Health Minister Sajid Javid and his counterparts in Scotland, Wales and Northern Ireland had written to the chief medical officers asking for further advice, "including on educational impacts", and the decision could be reversed in a matter of days or weeks.
The UK decision came as Australia's equivalent body, the Therapeutic Goods Administration (TGA), yesterday approved the use of Moderna's vaccine for use by children as young as 12.
It is the second vaccine after Pfizer to be approved by the TGA and the final hurdle - approval by the Australian Technical Advisory Group on Immunisation - is expected to be cleared later this week.
Mr Hunt said the rollout of Moderna and Pfizer for 12 to 15-year-olds would "offer them the best protection possible and help get them back into classrooms safely, as soon as possible". The Doherty Institute modelled how to begin reopening Australia, while maintaining non-lockdown health measures such as masks, when 70 and then 80 per cent of over 16s were vaccinated.
"Vaccinating 12 to 15-year-olds is over and above what was presumed in the Doherty modelling," Mr Hunt noted. "This is an important next step, vaccinations for all 12- to 15-year-olds will open on September 13."
TGA head Professor John Skerritt said the approval of the Moderna vaccine for children aged 12 and older was based on "evidence of strong ability for these vaccines to raise just as good if not stronger immunological responses as it does in young adults and older groups".
Professor Skerritt pointed out the UK government had ordered a review of the JCVI decision and "we may hear a different decision coming from the UK in the coming week".
University of Sydney infectious diseases paediatrician Professor Robert Booy said the UK was still recommending vaccination for the five to 10 per cent of children in the UK who had underlying condition or increased risk including "Down's syndrome, cerebral palsy and immune deficiency".
Nigel Curtis, an infectious disease physician at the Murdoch Children's Research Institute, said the JCVI's advice underscored the "complexity of the decisions" about vaccination.
"The risk of disease and death from COVID-19 is very low in children, and is still lower in adolescents than adults. But any harms from the vaccine are also very low," he said.
"The JCVI looked only at the relative harms to the individual, whereas other countries such as Australia has included considerations such as benefits of keeping schools open and the fact that Australian teenagers have not been exposed in large numbers." with Reuters
CREDIT: James Massola, Lucy Carroll and Latika Bourke

Premier’s week of confusing messages

Publication info: The Courier - Mail ; Brisbane, Qld. [Brisbane, Qld]. 04 Sep 2021: 5.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/premier-s-week-confusing-messages/docview/2569274430/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=13225235&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Premier%E2%80%99s+week+of+confusing+messages&amp;jtitle=The+Courier+-+Mail&amp;pubname=The+Courier+-+Mail&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Premier%26rsquo%3Bs+week+of+confusing+messages&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=5&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: STEVEN Miles doesn’t want Queenslanders to “fall for Scott Morrison’s marketing tactics” around opening up Australia.
He says the Doherty modelling is “much more complex than a number and a simple three-word slogan”.
I wonder if he had those pearls of wisdom for his own leader, who this week led Queensland through a mire of confusing messaging, scary warnings of impending death and imagery of sick kids, all the while trumpeting her own three-word slogan of “keeping Queenslanders safe”.
Because it wasn't exactly a week of informed and constructive public debate down on George St either.
It might have been different if Palaszczuk had just stood up on Tuesday and apologised for the fact football WAGs were allowed to fly into the state over locked-out Queenslanders – something she ended up doing anyway, just four days late.
Instead, the Premier let her chief health officer wear the fault and left her to defend her own Twitter death warnings at a long press conference she didn’t attend herself.
Because Twitter is definitely the best place for public debate, not a press conference. Right?
Oh, the hypocrisy.
Palaszczuk was much more measured yesterday, using the press conference to try to reset after the horror week and call for a more nuanced debate on living with Covid. That’s not only best for public policy, but best for her after she was left so isolated this week by medical experts and federal Labor colleagues, and so politically outplayed by Canberra.
CREDIT: JESSICA MARSZALEK; ANALYSIS

SA backs national cabinet path out of lockdowns

Author: Penberthy, David

Publication info: The Australian (Online) ; Canberra, A.C.T. [Canberra, A.C.T]. 02 Sep 2021.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/sa-backs-national-cabinet-path-out-lockdowns/docview/2568398698/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=Penberthy%2C+David&amp;aulast=Penberthy&amp;issn=&amp;isbn=&amp;title=SA+backs+national+cabinet+path+out+of+lockdowns&amp;jtitle=The+Australian+%28Online%29&amp;pubname=The+Australian+%28Online%29&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=SA+backs+national+cabinet+path+out+of+lockdowns&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: With other state leaders now walking away from the national cabinet plan framed around the Doherty modelling, the SA Premier said a consensus approach was crucial and that the scientific advice should unite the nation.
“We do have expert advice from Doherty, they pull it together from other experts right around the country,” Mr Marshall said.
“It’s a consensus model and it’s one that we in South Australian 100 per cent signed up to. We have listened to the experts, the evidence, the science, since day one here in SA. I think it’s put us in really good stead.”
But Mr Marshall said the country was now coming to a point where higher vaccination rates meant statewide lockdowns and whole-of-state border closures should no longer be used.
“If you are not going to have lockdowns you have to have higher vaccination rates and that’s what we are committed to in SA,” he said.
“When we get to 80 per cent which I hope is going to be in the coming months we will not be having statewide lockdowns. That’s the most punishing thing when you have got to put people in their own state into seven-day lockdowns. That will become a thing of the past.”
Mr Marshall reassured South Australians that he did not want to see any more lockdowns once the vaccination rate reached 80 per cent.
“It doesn’t mean that when we get a positive case we will just say ‘oh well, let that go through’,” he said.
“We will still do what we call test, trace, isolate and quarantine, so if you are infected we will look at those close contacts and put them into isolation.
“We don’t want it going through our state, but we do know that the transmission potential massively reduces once we get to 80 per cent of the adult population having this double dose of the vaccine.”
Despite having supported the imposition of tough border closures by his Covid team headed by Police Commissioner Grant Stevens, Mr Marshall said he did not want statewide border closures to continue.
He said the caveat to the removal of statewide lockdowns was that some interstate local government areas could still be precluded from travel at times when outbreaks occurred.
However, he said this could be managed in future with a more targeted approach than the blunt force of statewide travel bans.
“We will move to a more nuanced approach where instead of looking out a whole state we will say this LGA has got a breakout or a cluster,” he said.
“When people are putting in an application to come in, we will say these LGAs are excluded. But I think we will be moving away from whole of state lockdowns. The problem with the situation as it is at the moment is you really only know the actual situation of what’s going on in a state 14 days after it’s occurred. So you have to extrapolate because this is just such a transmissible version of the disease. But as the vaccination rate goes up, it’s not as transmissible. It reduces from eight times down to one or one and a half times.”
While refusing to take potshots at other state leaders, the SA Premier said the divergent approaches being taken in WA and Queensland made for “an interesting situation”, and joked that South Australia still remained part of the Federation.
“We are still signed up to the Federation, it’s a good system,” he said.
“It comes under a bit of stress every now and again but if you look at the systems of government around the world ours stands up pretty well to most.”

Premier’s alarm for children criticised

Publication info: The Cairns Post ; Cairns, Qld. [Cairns, Qld]. 02 Sep 2021: 5.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/premier-s-alarm-children-criticised/docview/2568094311/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=13228587&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Premier%E2%80%99s+alarm+for+children+criticised&amp;jtitle=The+Cairns+Post&amp;pubname=The+Cairns+Post&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Premier%26rsquo%3Bs+alarm+for+children+criticised&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=5&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: PREMIER Annastacia Palaszczuk has been accused of “scaremongering” by political foes and lacking common sense by “appalled” top doctors, as she seized on children’s welfare as the reason she still can’t lay out a plan for reopening the state.
Ms Palaszczuk appealed to parents, grandparents, aunts and uncles on Wednesday as she declared the fate of children was “the most serious issue that our country will face” and opening up would be exposing the most vulnerable.
After committing to a national cabinet plan to relax restrictions last month, the Premier said she now needed extra Doherty Institute modelling to show how children would fare before she could tell Queenslanders what life would look like when vaccination rates reached 80 per cent.
“Unless there is an answer on how these young people are going to be vaccinated, you are putting the most vulnerable population at risk,” she said.
“So anyone who has grandchildren, or young children, or nephews or nieces know how that plays on people’s minds.” But the comments were questioned by health experts, who said keeping borders shut to protect children was “not sensible”.
Veteran paediatrician and vaccine expert Professor Robert Booy, who is also a member of the national Immunisation Coalition, said: “I have been a paediatrician and have worked in the promotion of vaccinations for decades.
“If I thought young children needed urgent vaccination, I would say so. “Keeping borders shut because of the children is not a sensible measure.” An alert was issued for southern parts of the state after a truck driver with Covid travelled over the border.
CREDIT: Jessica Marszalek; Jackie Sinnerton; Madura McCormack

Subject: Immunization

Caution over national reopening plan

Publication info: The Canberra Times ; Canberra, A.C.T. [Canberra, A.C.T]. 01 Sep 2021: 10.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/caution-over-national-reopening-plan/docview/2566514015/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=01576925&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Caution+over+national+reopening+plan&amp;jtitle=The+Canberra+Times&amp;pubname=The+Canberra+Times&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Caution+over+national+reopening+plan&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=10&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: From Page 1 Mr Morrison's position on Tuesday more closely aligns with the national roadmap as it is written, which acknowledges that at least some basic restrictions and public health measures would be required even with 80 per cent of the adult population vaccinated.
Lockdowns would be "less likely but possible" at 70 per cent, and would still be an option - even if only in highly targeted circumstances - at 80 per cent.
"The public health social measures, they will continue," he said.
"There is not a time that we are contemplating where we move into Phase B and Phase C [of the plan] that they are not part of our management of our Covid response."
Mr Morrison conducted a local radio blitz in Covid-free states such as SA, Tasmania and WA on Tuesday, in an attempt to explain the national plan to populations wary about reopening their borders.
Sydney's ever-worsening Delta outbreak has caused widespread anxiety about the national reopening plan, and raised questions about whether key assumptions in the Doherty Institute modelling which underpins the roadmap can still be trusted.
Mr Morrison on Tuesday wouldn't be drawn on whether states should be shutting state borders once the vaccination targets were met, but conceded it was ultimately a matter for them.
However, he noted that health and economic advice had warned that imposing lockdowns at 80 per cent vaccine coverage would do "more harm than good".
Mr Barr this week said that reopening at 70 per cent vaccination coverage was "not safe" and discussion around easing restrictions should focus on the 80 per cent mark.
The ACT has set higher vaccination targets than the rest of the country, with Mr Barr hopeful 90 per cent of all Canberrans will be vaccinated by Christmas.
The lingering tension over the national strategy to reopen the country played out as the federal government announced it had struck a "dose swap" deal with Singapore.
Under the deal, Australia will receive 500,000 Pfizer doses from Singapore in September, before sending the same amount back to the south-east Asian city-state in December.
Mr Morrison said the additional doses would be distributed on a per capita basis to GP clinics and state vaccination hubs around the country, rather than channeled into areas facing Covid outbreaks.
CREDIT:

Caution over national reopening plan

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/caution-over-national-reopening-plan/docview/2566513642/se-2?accountid=13552

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=01576925&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Caution+over+national+reopening+plan&amp;jtitle=The+Canberra+Times&amp;pubname=The+Canberra+Times&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Caution+over+national+reopening+plan&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=10&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

WE NEED A PLAN

Publication info: Herald Sun ; Melbourne, Vic. [Melbourne, Vic]. 30 Aug 2021: 7.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/we-need-plan/docview/2565929999/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=10383433&amp;isbn=&amp;title=WE+NEED+A+PLAN&amp;jtitle=Herald+Sun&amp;pubname=Herald+Sun&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=WE+NEED+A+PLAN&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=7&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: VICTORIA’s crippling sixth lockdown will be extended with no end date in sight, forcing industry leaders to demand the Premier detail a “realistic” road map that offers “hope” instead of more despair for the state.
Daniel Andrews on Sunday said lockdown wouldn’t end on Thursday and refused to say how low case numbers would need to be to begin easing restrictions, sparking fears stay-at-home orders could drag until mid-November, when Victoria is due to reach 80 per cent vaccination.
Melbourne has now spent 211 days in hard lockdown and the week-long “circuit breaker” is now in its 26th day.
With 92 new Covid cases recorded on Sunday, Mr Andrews said: “We still have too many cases that are in the community for too long for us to be able to open up.
“We acted early but I’m not here to tell people this is easy, it’s not, it’s bloody hard.” But the Opposition said the state was being held “hostage” to a zero-case strategy, and the mental health harm caused by lockdown was now at alarming levels.
Victorian Chamber of Commerce and Industry chief executive Paul Guerra said businesses were in crisis and a road map out of lockdown that was “realistic and full of hope” was essential.
He said this could include reopening municipalities that were Covid-free, 24-hour vaccination hubs and kids back at school when vaccination rates hit 60 per cent.
“This lockdown is six and out for many, but for those that make it through, we need a plan,” Mr Guerra said.
“The state needs to articulate a reopening plan based on national cabinet’s road map and Doherty Institute modelling.” Mr Guerra said the path out needed to be detailed and even more ambitious than the state’s road map to recovery after the second wave.
“We are on track to have 70 per cent of people with their first jab in mid-October,” Mr Guerra said. “Why don’t we be bold and declare that from Caulfield Cup day and beyond crowds at race days can be at 50 per cent.” The Herald Sun believes that Mr Andrews expressed strong support for the national reopening plan during a phone call with Prime Minister Scott Morrison on Saturday.
Mr Andrews said he would make an announcement this week on any changes to restrictions, after receiving advice from the chief health officer.
But when asked how low cases would need to be to ease the current rules, he would only say “as low as we can get them”.
Unlike NSW, the Premier has not announced a plan for returning children to school.
State Opposition Leader Michael O’Brien said it was not feasible for the Premier to keep chasing zero cases.
“It is basically holding the whole of Victoria hostage to something which is practically unachievable, and is doing more damage in the meantime,” Mr O’Brien said.
“The amount of mental health harm, the amount of suicide attempts and certainly the number of suicides is going up because of these lockdowns.” Another $700m a week will be wiped from the balance sheet, as the engine room of the state’s economy struggles to stay afloat.
“Small businesses are just hanging on right now, they need hope,” federal Treasurer Josh Frydenberg said.
“They need to know that the plan agreed at national cabinet will be implemented, so they can plan for their futures.” Mr Frydenberg said he had a good working relationship with his Victorian counterpart, and together they had provided more than $2bn in economic support this lockdown. However, a school holiday cash splash that tourism operators rely on remains in jeopardy.
If Greater Melbourne and NSW remain in lockdown, a whopping $1.9bn is estimated to be lost over the fortnight from September 18.
Victorian Tourism Industry Council chief executive Felicia Mariani said a road map and a significant step-change to business support measures was required, if they were to survive this latest setback.
“These current grant programs, however, are sadly not going to save businesses from closures that now seem imminent,” Ms Mariani said.
“Businesses in the visitor economy right across the state are struggling under the weight of this latest lockdown and hope is waning that they will ever recover from mounting losses.” Father of three Chris Papas said families needed certainty about when students could return to the classroom.
“If the kids aren’t back by the end of term four it is going to be disastrous for their mental health, surely there are some measures the government can put in place,” he said.
Jodie Smith was forced to cancel her wedding this month, after the state was plunged into its sixth lockdown, and said they hadn’t rebooked as it was too hard to set a date.
“It would be nice to have certainty when we can look to plan a wedding date and a clear plan when we are going to have functions,” she said. “It has been pretty heartbreaking to plan everything and just undo it all at the last minute.” jade.gailberger@news.com.au EDITORIAL, OPINION: PAGES 22-23
CREDIT: JADE GAILBERGER MITCH RYAN

Subject: Mental health; Immunization; Tourism

Herald Sun

Publication info: Herald Sun ; Melbourne, Vic. [Melbourne, Vic]. 30 Aug 2021: 22.

https://login.ezproxy.lib.rmit.edu.au/login?url=https://www.proquest.com/newspapers/herald-sun/docview/2565929433/se-2?accountid=13552

Abstract: None available.

Links: https://libkey.io/libraries/1057/openurl?genre=article&amp;au=&amp;aulast=&amp;issn=10383433&amp;isbn=&amp;title=Herald+Sun&amp;jtitle=Herald+Sun&amp;pubname=Herald+Sun&amp;btitle=&amp;atitle=Herald+Sun&amp;volume=&amp;issue=&amp;spage=22&amp;date=2021&amp;doi=&amp;sid=ProQuest

Full text: Locking down without a plan AS Melbourne today enters a 26th day of what was supposed to be a week-long circuit-breaker lockdown and our 211th day of stay-at-home orders, Victorians are demanding a clear plan out of this crushing Covid stalemate.
More than 6.6 million Victorians have done the hard yards over the past 18 months of pandemic pandemonium but even now, after all the costs and lost time, there is no clear vision forward other than blunt lockdowns and a distant vaccine horizon.
Tens of thousands of businesses have been hammered, many ruined, families have been separated, education for an entire generation has been disrupted and mental health issues are at record levels.
Melburnians have now endured a cumulative lockdown second in length only the Argentine capital Buenos Aires, in a country which relaxed a range of restrictions this month even though it has almost 7000 cases and 170 deaths each day.
Yesterday, Victoria recorded a worrying increase in community-acquired daily cases to 92 and New South Wales had an alarming new-record of 1218 cases, but the wide disparity in infection statistics was not the only difference between the two states.
As Victorian Premier Daniel Andrews faced the cameras to confirm Melbourne’s scheduled end to lockdown this Thursday would be again extended, NSW Premier Gladys Berejiklian said her state, now at the halfway mark to 70 per cent of all adults fully vaccinated, would “show the way” on how to live with Covid.
While Victoria must ensure it does not follow NSW into its exponential growth in cases — that has put 813 people currently in hospital, including 126 in intensive care — there is at least some plan north of the Murray for selected reopening and targeted relaxation.
The NSW plan to give back some freedoms is centred on rewarding double-vaccinated people, a policy that needs to be adopted here.
While the countrywide vision for reopening agreed to at national cabinet, based on Doherty Institute modelling, maps out a longer-term way forward, there has to be scope for returning some liberties and livelihoods before the target 70 and then 80 per cent full vaccination triggers that are still months away.
As the Sydney outbreak bled into regional NSW and community infections continued to spiral, the focus there has been on vaccination rates rather than just daily infection tallies.
Certainly, the federal acceleration of vaccine stocks into NSW helped them reach almost 835,000 doses last week, but Victoria must increase its supplies of AstraZeneca and now push for further shipments of Pfizer to meet our Delta challenge.
On the current trajectory, NSW is expected to reach 70 per cent full vaccination of eligible adults by as early as the first week of October, weeks before Victoria hits the same mark.
We have got to do better and simply blaming supplies solves nothing — we need to increase AstraZeneca messaging, more localised, pop-up clinics and a more proactive educational push through GPs and pharmacies is needed, particularly in Melbourne’s north and western suburbs that are carrying about 500 of the 773 current community cases.
Up to five people will be allowed to gather outdoors for recreation outside greater Sydney hotspot municipalities from mid-September and an hour of recreation on top of the hour of exercise within suburbs of concern for those who have been vaccinated.
Proof of vaccination on the digital myGov website will be required to be shown as part of the health order requirements.
And in a staggered approach, NSW students will return to face-to-face learning in schools beginning from October 25.
Premier Andrews yesterday said Victorians could still wrench back Delta case numbers by strictly adhering to stay-at-home restrictions and getting tested at the earliest sign of symptoms.
There was still a chance we could wrest back control in coming weeks, he insisted.
But there must be a more nuanced approach to offer reason for optimism and not just endless compliance.
Balancing what is being demanded of Victorians with relaxation of restrictions wherever and whenever possible must form part of the plan, together with catching up on strong but sub-optimal vaccination rates.
Much of regional Victoria could be released from many restrictions even now. And there is still a complete absence of a clear timeline for wider returns to in-class schooling in this state, community sport and re-engagement in workplaces.
Certainly, large swaths of greater Melbourne and some regional areas, particularly Shepparton, remain on a knife’s edge in seeking to contain local infections.
But that does not excuse the Andrews government for its failure to set out a clear, achievable way forward and to specify what reduced case numbers will allow us to move beyond captivity and constraint.
Clear vision is, after all, what defines leadership. Instead, in the days leading up to this Thursday when lockdown was supposed to end, Victorians will be told to hunker down longer and hope some freedoms will be restored, sometime.

Subject: Vaccines; Immunization

Company / organization: Name: AstraZeneca; NAICS: 325412
